GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13176

THE GEOLOGISTS REGISTRATION ACT

( No. 10 of 1993)

APPOINTMENT OF MEMBERS OF THE GEOLOGISTS REGISTRATION BOARD

IN  EXERCISE  of  the  powers  conferred  by  section  3  (3)  of  the Geologists  Registration  Act,  and  in  particular,  paragraph  1  of  the Schedule thereto, the Minister for Environment and Mineral Resources appoints-

Under paragraph (1) (2) ( a )-

Benard Kipsang Rop (Dr.)-Three (3) years. Martin Mwaisakenyi Heya-One (1) year. Harie Kinosthe Ndung'u-Two (2) years.

Under paragraph 1 (2) ( b )-

Felix Nyongesa Mutunguti-One (1) year.

Gladys Karegi Kianji-One (1) year.

to  be  members  of  the  Geologists  Registration  Board,  for  the  period respectively specified, with effect from 1st November, 2009.

Dated the 1st December, 2009.

J. N. MICHUKI,

Minister for Environment and Mineral Resources.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13177

THE NATIONAL MUSEUMS AND HERITAGE ACT ( No. 6 of 2006)

APPOINTMENT

IN  EXERCISE  of  the  powers  conferred  by  section  6  of  the National Museums and Heritage Act, 2006, the Minister of State for National Heritage and Culture appoints-

Under subsection (1) (b)

Fleur Ng'weno Rashid Abdi Aman (Dr.) Ephraim Wachira Wahome (Dr.)

Under subsection (1) (f)

Charles Nyakweba

Under subsection (1) (h)

Muriithi Ndegwa to be members of the Board of the National Museums of Kenya, for a period of three years with effect from 9th September, 2009.

Dated the 7th December, 2009.

WILLIAM OLE NTIMAMA,

Minister of State for National Heritage and Culture.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13178

THE KENYA NATIONAL LIBRARY SERVICE BOARD ACT ( Cap. 225)

APPOINTMENT

IN  EXERCISE  of  the  powers  conferred  by  section  6  (2)  of  the Kenya National Library Board Act, the Minister of State for National Heritage and Culture appoints-

RICHARD M. ATUTI

to be the Director of the Kenya National Library Service for a term of three (3) years with effect from 1st September, 2009. The appointment of Irene Muthoni Kibandi* is revoked.

Dated the 7th December, 2009.

WILLIAM OLE NTIMAMA,

Minister of State for National Heritage and Culture.

*G. N. 6325/06.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13179

THE LABOUR RELATIONS ACT ( No. 14 of 2007)

COLLECTION OF AGENCY FEES

IN  EXERCISE  of  the  conferred  by  section  49  of  the  Labour Relations Act, No. 14 of 2007, the Minister for Labour:

( a ) Orders  Messrs.  Kenya  Industrial  Research  and  Development Institute;

(i)  To deduct every month the sum of Ksh. 120 in respect of trade union agency fees from the basic wages of his/her employees who are covered by the terms and conditions of the concluded Collective  Bargaining  Agreement  and  are  not  members  of Union  of  National  Research  and  Allied  Institutes  Staff  of Kenya (UNRISK).

(ii) To  pay  within  ten  (10)  days  of  the  deduction  the  total  sums deducted  by  a  crossed  cheque  made  payable  to  Union  of National Research and Allied Institutes Staff of Kenya (UNRISK) into the Union's account number 234793836 at the Kenya Commercial Bank Limited, Moi Avenue Branch, P.O. Box 30081, Nairobi.

(iii)To make returns to the Registrar of Trade Unions at P.O. Box 40326,  Nairobi  within  one  (1)  month  of making  all the payments to the union and to that organization.

Dated the 15th October, 2009.

M. K. KIYONG'A, Minister for Labour.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13180

THE CRIMINAL PROCEDURE CODE

( Cap. 75)

APPOINTMENT

IN  EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section  85  (1)  of  the Criminal Procedure Code, the Attorney-General appoints-

Benjamin M. Wambua, Dickson M. Onsongo, Eric K. Rotich, Linus L. Murithi, Paul M. Mwangangi, Fidelis M. Kavoi, David M. Nzioka, John B. Mulongo, to  be  public  prosecutors  for  the  purposes  of  cases  arising  under  the Immigration Act (Cap. 172).

Dated the 3rd December, 2009.

S. A. WAKO, Attorney-General.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13181

THE CHILDREN ACT

( No. 8 of 2001)

APPOINTMENT

IN EXERCISE of the powers conferred by section 73 ( d ) (ii) of the Children Act, 2001, the Chief Justice appoints-

BENSON N. IRERI

Resident Magistrate at Kibera, to preside over cases involving children in respect of Nairobi Province, with effect from 1st December, 2009.

Dated the 30th November, 2009.

J. E. GICHERU, Chief Justice.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13183

THE REGISTRATION OF TITLES ACT

( Cap. 281, section 71)

ISSUE OF A PROVISIONAL CERTIFICATE

WHEREAS  Edina  Cherop  Yego,  the  administrator  of  the  estate  of Daniel  Kibiwott  Yego  (deceased),  of  P.O.  Box  5401,  Nairobi  in  the Republic of Kenya, is  the registered proprietor lessee of that piece of land known as L.R. No. 5795(Orig. No.1920/1), situate in the north of Kitale Municipality, by virtue of a certificate of title registered as I.R. 1609/1,  and  whereas  sufficient  evidence  has  been  adduced  to  show that  the  said  certificate  of  title  issued  thereof  has  been  lost,  notice  is given that after the expiration of ninety (90) days from the date hereof, I shall issue a provisional certificate of title provided that no objection has been received within that period.

Dated the 11th December, 2009.

C. N. KITUYI, Registrar of Titles, Nairobi.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13189

THE REGISTRATION OF TITLES ACT ( Cap. 281)

REGISTRATION OF INSTRUMENT

WHEREAS (1) Ezekiel Barngetuny and (2) Joel Muthusi Mbithi, both of P.O. Box 36, Kapsabet in the Republic of Kenya, are registered proprietors  lessees  of  that  piece  of  land  containing  1954.0  acres  less road  reserve  or  thereabout,  known  as  L.R.  No.  7300,  situate  in  the north east of Muhoroni Township, held under grant registered as I.R. 4900/1, and whereas Agricultural Finance corporation, a state corporation  having  its  registered  office  at  Nairobi,  has  executed instruments  of  notification  of  discharges  and  discharge  of  charge  in favour of the said (1) Ezekiel Barngetuny and (2) Joel Muthusi Mbithi, and whereas affidavits have been filled in terms of section 65 (1) ( h ) of the said Act, declaring that the said grant registered as No. I.R 4900/1 is not available for registration, notice is given that after the expiration of  fourteen  (14)  days  from  the  date  hereof  provided  that  no  valid objection  has  been  received  within  that  period,  I  intend  to  dispense with the production of the said grant and proceed with the registration of the said instruments of notification of discharge and discharges of charge.

Dated the 11th December, 2009.

C. S. MAINA, Registrar of Titles, Nairobi.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13190

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13455

THE ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

( No. 8 of 1999)

THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED STREAM CANALIZATION AND REALIGNMENT ON L.R. NO. 3734/549/45 ALONG CHALBI DRIVE, LAVINGTON, NAIROBI

INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of Environmental  (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National  Environment  Management Authority (NEMA) has received an Environmental Impact Assessment Study Report for the implementation of the Proposed Stream Canalization and Realignment on L.R. NO. 3734/549/45 Along Chalbi Drive, Lavington, Nairobi.

The  proponent  intends  to  divert  the  Katina  river  channel  (which flows in the middle of the plot), through an appropriately designed box channel running parallel to the northern boundary of the plot without disturbing the existing NCC sewer line.

The  project anticipates the  following  impacts  and mitigation measures:-

Possible Impacts | Mitigation Measures
Protection of the stream canal |  CCN and Nairobi Water and Sewerage company should ensure all sewer waste in the slums is connected to the improved sewer system  Ensure all the recharge areas on the lower part of the plot are not blocked  The proper anti-pollution measures must be put in place  Consider maximum flood levels  Follow all NEMA, WRMA and CCN recommendations  Comply with all the relevant provisions of the water Act.  Regular inspection of the canalised stream  Water quality measurements
Changes in hydrology/ impended drainage |  Proper Installation of drainage structures  Install cascades to break the impact of water flowing in the drains  Ensure efficiency of drainage structures trough proper design and maintenance  Provide gratings to the drainage channels  Regular checks on any sludge along drainage channels  Control earthworks
Soil erosion |  Rehabilitate degraded environment to avoid siltation and wash offs.  Compact loose soils and Landscaping  Ensure management of excavation activities  Control activities especially during rainy conditions  Provide soil erosion control and conservation structures where necessary.  Proper disposal of excavated loose soil

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 Control speed and operation of construction vehicles

Air pollution through dust and gaseous emissions

 Prohibit idling of vehicles

 Water  should  be  sprayed  during  the construction phase of excavated areas

 Regular  maintenance  of  construction plant and equipment

 Engage sensitive construction workers.

 Proper use of PPEs

 Sensitize drivers of construction machinery on effects of noise

Noise pollution

 Maintain plant equipment (if present/used)

 Construction  activities  to  be  restricted to daytime

 Workers in the vicinity of or involved in  high-level  noise  to  wear  respective safety & protective gear i.e. earplugs & earmuffs

 Appropriate selection of machinery

 Proper  storage,  handling  and  disposal of  new  oil  and  used  oil  and  related wastes

Oil pollution

 Maintain plant and equipment to avoid leaks

 Maintenance  of  construction  vehicles should be carried out in the contractors yard (off the site)

 Management  of  water  usage.  Avoid unnecessary  wastage  especially  at  the car washing bay

Water resource

 Recycling of water during construction phase where possible

 Use of water conservation signs at the wash rooms and install water conserving taps



 Special attention should be paid to the sanitary facilities on site especially disposal of human waste.

Contractors lay down area

 Garbage  should  be  disposed  off in accordance with local Council requirements

Road safety

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13156

THE ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

(No. 8 of 1999)

THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED SEWER LINE DIVERSION OF THE EPZA SEWER LINE LOCATED BETWEEN PLOT NUMBERS: LR. 337/976, LR.337/1074 AND LR 337/2719 IN ATHI RIVER

INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of Environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority  (NEMA)  has  received  an  Environmental Impact  Assessment  Study  Report  for  the  implementation  of  the Proposed Sewer Line Diversion of the Epza Sewer Line.

The proponent intends to create a sewage diversion of around 110 meters  for  its  factory  expansion  project  on  No.  LR.  337/2719.  The diversion  is  to  provide  space  for  the  factory  expansion.  The  site  is located  in  Athi  River  in  Mavoko  Municipality.  The  site  is  located between Plot Numbers: 337/976, 337/1074 337/2719.

The  project anticipates the  following  impacts  and mitigation measures:

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 Ascertain the location of all the water pipes, electrical installation and other possible interferences within the area of sewer construction.

Location

 Elevations  should  be  taken  at  intervals  in case of change of gradient.

 Bench marks should be placed at convenient intervals for use during construction.

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 A specially equipped tractor will be required for this section and properly trained staff by the contractor

Trenching

 A  suitable  bedding  for  the  sewer  concrete pipes will be required and they should maintain the necessary grade.

Foundations

 Acceptable  grading  as  per  the  consultants expert should be provided

 If  rock is present it should be removed to a depth of 4 to 6 inches below the bottom of the pipes' placement. if the soil is soft it will have to be stabilized with a packed layer of gravel or broken rock

 Frequently the trench will collect water especially because we are in the rainy season

Removing Water

 The  sewer  will  have  to  be  layed  from  the lowest part of the line to permit the water to flow away  from the completed sections centrifugal  pumps  will  be  required    to  be used for dewatering the trench.

 For muddy material a diaphragm pump will be required.

 For wet sections well points will be used or a  drain  with  open  joints    and  bedded  with gravel built underneath the sewer to remove the water.

 The concrete pipes will have to be placed in their  exact  positions,  the  elevation  of  the pipes  will  be  checked  and  if  correct  a  joint will be made.

Placing the concrete pipes

 Where an immediate connection is not made,  a  vitrified  -  clay  will  have  to  be connected  to the branch  bell to prevent entrance of dirt or ground water.

 Branches  or  slants,  for  factory  connections must be installed at the proper locations and with the stubs pointing to the correct side of the location.

Provision for Factory Connections

 The position decided on, may be marked  by a  stake  just  in  advance  of  concrete  pipe laying.

 Because of the current construction activities  in  the  area,  the  need  for  a  firm backfill  will  be  required  because  of  the traffic issue

Backfilling

 Compaction will be required during backfill with sand or gravel backfill.

 Careful, skilled and continuous inspection of every  phase  of  sewer  construction  will  be required

Inspection

 Inspection will include examining each section  of  the  concrete  pipe  to  make  sure that it is unbroken and usable, checking the position  of  the  pipes  in  the  trench  for  line and  grade,  watching  the  forming  of  the joints, requiring proper bedding and backfill placement,  determine  the  need  for  trench drainage  to  ensure  that  good  work  can  be done, grade boards and gradient lines should be checked frequently for accuracy.

 As soon as each section is completed, tests should be conducted to determine the level of infiltration or leakage into the sewer.

Measuring Infiltration

 An exfiltration test will be required.

 Because sewers are buried after construction careful records will be required during construction.

Record Keeping

 The  records  should  show  the  location  and size and the starting and ending points.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

(e) The  Director-General,  National  Environment  Management Authority, Popo Road, off Mombasa Road, P.O. Box 6783900200, Nairobi.

(f) The  Permanent  Secretary,  Ministry  of  Environment  and Natural Resources, National Hospital Insurance Fund Building, Community, 4th Floor, P.O. Box 30521, Nairobi.

(g) Provincial Director of Environment, Nairobi Province.

(h) District Environment Officer, Nairobi West District.

The National Environment Management Authority invites members  of  the  public  to  submit  oral  or  written  comments  within thirty  (30)  days  from  the  date  of  publication  of  this  notice  to  the Director-General,  National  Environment  Management  Authority,  to assist the authority in the approval process of the project.

Dated the 12th November, 2009.

B. M. LANGWEN, for Director-General, National Environment Management Authority.

THE NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED NATIONAL CO-OPERATIVE HOUSING UNION (NACHU) PRESTIGE HOUSING SCHEME ON L.R. No. 23405 MAVOKO MUNICIPAL COUNCIL

INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority  (NEMA)  has  received  an  Environmental Impact  Assessment  Study  Report  for  the  implementation  of  the proposed  National  Co-operative  Housing  Union  (NACHU)  prestige Housing Scheme.

The  proposed  project  will  comprise  of  Type  A  semi  detached luxury  masionettes  housed  on  70  No.  plots  of  minimum  size  21.0  x 8.5m, each maisonnette is to have a plinth area of 100m². The second proposal will have Type B and will be composed of flats planned and arranged in 10 No. Each block is to accommodate 16 No. flats with a plinth area of 102.0m² per flat. The proposed project will be located on L.R. No. 23405 Mavoko Municipal Council.

The  project anticipates the  following  impacts  and mitigation measures:

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 Excavating only necessary areas.

Soil

 Containment of soil heaps to prevent. erosion  caused  by  runoffs,  wind  and  from machinery.

 Reduce the use of heavy machinery whenever possible.

 Use  of  light  machinery  at  the  site  during construction process.

 Leaving  trees  outside  designated  areas  of construction activities.

 Excavating only construction areas.

 Construction of drainage systems.

Water Resources

 Prevention  of  pollution  during  construction activities to  minimize effects that may arise during surface runoffs.

 Prevention  of  any  pollution  resulting  from construction activities.

 Instituting water savings strategies to minimize water use.

 Construction of drainage channels to ensure waste water handling.

 Ensure reuse of waste water by sprinkling at the site to reduce excessive dust.

Mitigation Measures

Possible Impacts

 Construction of leak proof drains.

 Instituting water saving strategies/practices.

 Landscaping of the construction site.

 Limiting construction traffic  movement and operation to efficient and necessary activities

Air and Noise pollution

 Routine  maintenance  of  vehicles  and  other machinery  to  be  used  during  construction process

 Minimizing  transportation  activities  to  day time only

 Erection of buffer fence to retain most of the noise to the construction site

 The  road  leading  to  the  site  be  sprinkled with water to mitigate excessive dust emission

 Limiting  construction  activities  to  day  time only

 Sensitize construction drivers and machinery operators  to  switch  off  engines  when  not being used.

 Regular serving of construction and transport  machinery  to  ensure  that  they  are in  good  working  condition  and  to  reduce emissions

 Use of commercial bill boards to keep construction activities out of sight from immediate neighborhood.

Visual Intrusion

 Fencing out the construction site.

 Landscaping and gardening to restore biodiversity  and  aesthetic  properties  of  the project site.

 Waste minimization by avoiding unsustainable construction practices.

Solid Waste

 Sorting of waste.

 Provision of dust bins to hold waste before disposal.

 Reuse  where  possible  or  sale  to  authorized waste handlers/collectors.

 Workers training on safety.

Occupational Health and safety

 Risk analysis for all activities, materials and equipment.

 Provision of protective clothing.

 Emergency response plan.

 Need for firefighting equipment to be made available on site.

 Inclusion of fire exit route.

 Effluent discharge shall be channeled to the main sewer line that serves the area.

Effluent discharge

 All  effluent  to  meet  NEMA  standards  for discharge to a sewer line.

 Provision  of  adequate  spatial  conditions  in the  project  design  to  avoid  congestion  and related public health and social problems.

Public  nuisance  in form of smoke, smell and visual intrusion

 Provision of trade opportunities for residents and surrounding community.

 Construction of spacious driveways and walk ways.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

(a) The Director-General, National Environment Management Authority,  Popo  Road,  off  Mombasa  Road,  P.O.  Box 67839-00200, Nairobi.

GAZETTE NOTICE NO. 13158

THE ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AND CO-ORDINATION ACT

NATIONAL ENVIRONMENT MANAGEMENT AUTHORITY

(No . 8 of 1999)

ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT STUDY REPORT FOR THE PROPOSED PROSPECTING AND MINING OF MANGANESE ORE AT GANZE, KILIFI DISTRICT

INVITATION OF PUBLIC COMMENTS

PURSUANT to regulation 21 of Environmental (Impact Assessment and Audit) Regulations, the National Environment Management  Authority (NEMA)  has  received an environmental impact assessment study report for the implementation of the proposed prospecting and mining of manganese ore at Ganze, Kilifi District.

The  proposed  project  entails  prospecting,  mining  and  sale  of manganese (Mn) ore. The project will be located in Ganze Location, Ganze Division, Kilifi District in Coast Province of Kenya and covers about 15 sq.km.

The  project anticipates the  following  impacts  and mitigation measures:-

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 PRANAAV  will undertake Alovera and adaptive  grass  planting  as  the  construction progresses to avoid the soil being washed or carried by wind.

Vegetation loss and Soil erosion

 Places of least vegetation cover  will be identified for the campsite and only construction points will be completely cleared to ensure minimum vegetative disturbance.

 Proper  roof  catchments  and  gutters  will  be put in place to control the possible increased runoff.

 Temporary storage tanks will be supplied to trap this water for irrigating planted vegetation.

 The Proponent will do landscaping, and fill the  depressions  including  borrow  pits  and disused quarries.

Ponding Risk from construction

 Pumping  of  water  into  suitably  designed drainage outlets into the seasonal stream will be ensured.

 The quality of the discharged water will be monitored in keeping with the Legal Notice 120, of 2006.

 Prompt compaction of loose soils and aggressive grass replanting will be implemented.

Air pollution from Dust and Engine exhaust gases

 The distance to the neared population concentration is about 1.5km. the impact of the dust on the surrounding people is therefore unlikely.

Possible Impacts

Mitigation Measures

 Water will be sprinkled on to the disturbed

 Dust screens will be erected to contain flying dust and employees/ construction workers will be provided with personal protective equipment (PPE), to reduce possible dust and noxious gas inhalation.

 Public movement through this mining spots will generally be restricted.

Obstruction by disposed Excavated Soil

 Emergency responses which might be hindered by the obstruction will be provided for by clear operating procedures.

 Most of the excavated materials will be used for  fill-ups  and  some  will  be  applied  in landscaping.

 The  staff  will  not  be  residing  on  site  but appropriate

Waste into the Environment

 sized potable septic tanks will be availed to staff during their working hours and to keep with the movement of operations.

 Quality standards will be adhered to through initial testing and periodic monitoring in line with  the  requirements  of  NEMA  contained in the Legal Notice 120, of 2006.

 Appropriate soakpits system will be constructed.

 The  proponent  will  ensure  that  it  enlists  a licensed  private  company  specialized  in  the handling oil and solid waste wherever necessary.

 Biodegradable kitchen waste will be composted on site for tree planting manure.

 A Good Housekeeping as part of the company policy will be implemented at the facility.

 The mining operations may stop temporarily during  the  very  wet  season  when  working the mines becomes difficult and dangerous.

Surface and Ground Water Contamination

 The project will have an adequate drainage, on site containment to minimise uncontrolled storm water.

 Well documented procedures for maintenance of the drainage system will be implemented and staff will be trained accordingly.

 Oil  waste  will  never  be  allowed  into  the environment; proper containment and accidental  spill  absorption  regime  will  be implemented at all time.

 Vegetative pollutant traps and continual monitoring of the waters on site and surrounding areas will form  part of the pollution control efforts by the company.

 The contractor will ensure that the operations of most of the machinery such as excavator,  loader  shovel  and  graders  are concentrated within 100m-radius and that all workers  are  provided  with  and  using  PPE such as earmuffs.

Noise pollution and Vibrations nuisance

 Vibrations and noise surveillance instruments  will  be  availed  periodically  to check on any excesses.

 Dust  containment  and  suction  systems  will be installed.

Health deterioration of facility workers off-pit soil to reduce flying dust.

 Use of PPEs will be strictly enforced.

 Welders  will  be  provided  with  respirators, eye  protections  and  dust  coats  to  minimize inhalations.

 Regular  medical  checks  will  be  done  and records maintained of the employees.

 Staff working at the site on permanent basis will have medical cover.

 Sanitation related education and practice will form part of the facility's regular routine,  to  avoid  incidences  of  infections such as cholera, bilharzias and malaria. Swapping  of  work  stations  for  staff  will reduce level exposure.

The full report of the proposed project is available for inspection during working hours at:

(a) The  Director-General,  National  Environment  Management Authority, Popo Road, off Mombasa Road, P.O. Box 6783900200, Nairobi.

(b) The  Permanent  Secretary,  Ministry  of  Environment  and Natural Resources, National Hospital Insurance Fund Building, Community, 4th Floor, P.O. Box 30521, Nairobi.

(c)     Provincial Director of Environment, Coast Province.

(d)     District Environment Officer, Kilifi District.

The National Environment Management Authority invites members  of  the  public  to  submit  oral  or  written  comments  within thirty  (30)  days  from  the  date  of  publication  of  this  notice  to  the Director-General,  National  Environment  Management  Authority,  to assist the authority in the approval process of the project.

Dated the 28th August, 2009.

B. M. LANGWEN, for Director-General,

National Environment Management Authority.

IMPORTANT NOTICE TO SUBSCRIBERS TO THE KENYA GAZETTE

THE following notes are for the guidance of persons submitting 'copy' for inclusion in the Kenya Gazette, Supplement , etc.:

The Kenya Gazette contains Notices of a general nature which do not affect  legislation.  They  are,  therefore,  submitted  to  the  Government Printer directly.

Legislative  Supplement contains  Rules  and  Regulations  which  are issued  by  the  Central  Government.  Because  of  this,  they  must  be submitted  to  the Government  Printer  through  the  office  of  the Attorney-General.

Bill  Supplement contains  Bills  which  are  for  introduction  in  the National Assembly.

Act Supplement contains Acts passed by the National Assembly.

All 'copy' submitted for publication should be prepared on one side of an A4  sheet  no  matter  how  small  the  Notice  is,  each  page  being  numbered  and should  be  typewritten  with  double  spacing.  Copy  should  be  clear,  legible  and contain no alterations.

Particular attention should be paid to the following points:

(i) Signature must be supported by rubber-stamping or typing the name of the signatory in capital letters.

(ii) Dates must be correct and filled in where necessary.

(iii) Care  should  be  taken  to  ensure  that  all  headings  to  Notices  and references to legislation are up to date and conform with the Revised Edition of the Laws of Kenya.

EXTRACT FROM THE CODE OF REGULATIONS, SECTION D-

Kenya Gazette

'D  34.  (1)  Communications  for  the Kenya  Gazette should  reach  the Government  Printer  not  later  than  9  a.m.  on  Friday  of  the  week  before publication is desired. The Government Printer will not publish communications received after that hour until the next subsequent issue of the Gazette.

Ministries will be required to pay for the Kenya Gazette and to meet the cost of advertising in it.

It  is  emphasized that these notes are for guidance only, but it is requested that  persons  submitting  copy  for  publication  first  satisfy  themselves  that  such copy is complete in every respect.
